Page 21 (type diary) http://wd3.herokuapp.com/pages/AWD0000i7i  ----------
  Hashtags: #friendly 
  9 Sep 1914 0
    unit:French Cavalry Division (61,10)
    reference:Beaurepaire farm Nr. Coupru, Aisne, France, September 10th 1914: Marched 04:15 to point north east of Coupru and from there to Epaux-Bezu, where there was a heavy cannonade on the hedges. There to Griselles (Grisolles) where guns are in action and German troops retiring north. The regiment was then sent to Chateau Montigny where German convoy and a large force of cavalry moving up the Latilly-Montcru road. 'B' squadron was sent to ridge onthe left flank but were heavily shelled and had some difficulty in geting up there. A French cavalry division came up on the right and packed on slowly after convoy. patrols to Oulchy and hartignes. Billeted at Montigny (la croix) at the farm at back of the chateau. (18,12)
  10 Sep 1914 20
    place:Coupru (52,23)

    unit:1 Brigade (20,28)
    unit:1 Division infantry (28,28)
    unit:French (53,28)
    reference:Montigny/La Croix chateau, Aisne, France, September 11th 1914: Marched 04:15 to Oulchy where were were passed by 1st brigade who were late. Halted until 08:00, thence to point 19 degrees/1 mile north of Saponay, where we awaited the arrival of 1st division infantry who(se) flank we are guarding. We then moved through Cuigny - Wallee - Cranaille and at 12:45 arrived at Loupeignes. Took up a position 1 mile north. French out in action against Mont Notre Dame. patrol to Journignes but had to retire as they nearly cut off. (A) storm came in at 15:30 and lasted until 17:00. Retired to billets at Loupeignes at 17;30. (13,29)

  11 Sep 1914 46
    unit:Two French batteries (31,48)
    activity:movement (24,49)
    place:Oulchy (41,49)
    place:Montigny La Croix Chateau (10,49)
    unit:3 Hussars (22,49)
    unit:1 Brigade (64,49)
    reference:Loupeigne, Aisne, France, September 12th 1914: Marched at  04:30 and reached point 13 degrees West of Quincy (sous-le-Mont) at 06:30. 3rd Hussars sent to gain high ground North of Ruesle were driven back by German infantry entrenched near Bazoches (sur-Vesles). Two French batteries spewed heavy fire from Mont-notre-Dame - to (the) consternation of a battalion who had walked into the Germans, thinking they were French. 09:30: move to Lesges where we arrived at 11:45  and remained in the line. Heavy firing all day. Left Lesges (at) 17:45 and marched through Lime - Braine, to Vaulxtin where we arrived in the night, wet through, and went into billets.   (14,49)

Page 22 (type diary) http://wd3.herokuapp.com/pages/AWD0000hwn  ----------
  13 Sep 1914 9
    reference:Vauxtin, Aisne, France, September 13th 1914: Marched at  06:40 to Epine de Vauxcere where we halted for hour, from there to LaCoeur des Moines Farm where we halted and off-saddled until 11:00. Information then received that 1st and 3rd brigades had crossed the Aisne at Pont D'Arcy and Bourg and have moved to point just South of Bourg. Moved to Revillion at 17:45.  Heavy cannonade on heights to Pont Aichy-Villers, Billeted at Revillion. (16,10)

  Hashtags: #Indian 
  25 Apr 1915 0
    reference:Vlamertinge, Ypres, Belgium, April 26th 1915: Remained in billet all the morning. At about 16:00received an order to be ready to march to trenches: 'E' of Ypres starting at 17:30. At 17:45 order was cancelled and regiment remain in billets for the night. Ready to move at half hour's notice. Attack of Lahore division was stopped opposite St. Julien. Northumberland brigade made progress and took St Julien but had to evacuate that place later. French attack advancing as far as Het Sas where street fighting was in progress.(The) French also re-took Lizerne but attack towards Steenstraat did not make much progress. 3rd and 5th cavalry brigades in 2nd line trenches in support of 1/27th division. (17,12)

  Hashtags: #horses 
  26 Apr 1915 0
    unit:13 Brigade (40,10)
    reference:Vlamertinge, Ypres, Belgium, April 27th 1915: Remained in billet during the morning. Situation reported to be normal. Germans still held Bridge head to North of Canal at Het Sas. During the evening Vlamertinge was shelled and the led horses of (the) Scots Greys suffered.Regiment march(ed) back to led horses just before dusk and received orders to be prepared to march to trenches near Ypres. Received orders to march at 23:00 and went via Vlamertinge and the outskirts of Ypres and took over 2nd line trenches near Wieltje. Regiment on left of 13th with 3rd Hussars on our right. Arrived at trenches at about 02:00 and spend the remainder of night improving them. (21,10)

  Hashtags: #aeroplane 
  27 Apr 1915 0
    reference:Wieltje, Ypres, Belgium, April 28th 1915: Remained in the trenches all day, Working party of 3 officers and 100 men paraded at 07:00 to dig new 2nd line trenches. They returned at 23:30. A disabled German aeroplane came over our lines at about 19:00, flying very low and slowly. Regiment commenced a heavy fire and the machine came to the ground about half (a mile) to the North East of our trenches. Pilot and observer were both captured. Heavy shelling all day.    (19,14)
    unit:Enemy plane grounded (31,14)

  4 Sep 1916 24
    reference:L'Offand near Hazebrouck, Nord, France, September 4th 1916 (continued): Exercise and Stables under squadron arrangements. The dismounted party of the regiment paraded at 09:15 at regimental headquarters and proceeded to Morbecque camp by motor lorries. Second Lieutentant Mitchell who had just rejoined the regiment from the 9th cavalry brigade, A.D.C, to General P.R.Kelly C.M.G, was in charge of the party. The party afterwards proceeded to the Somme and were encamped near Carnoy. they were utilised to make tracks up to the firing line for use of the 2nd cavalry division. (22,14)

  10 Apr 1917 0
    reference:Pas-en-Artois,pas de calais, france, April 12th 1917: Captain P.H. Compton was admitted to hospital. The regiment paraded at 11:30 and proceeded via Le Bac du Nord -Beaumetz le Luges- La herliere to Pas, going into the same bivouac as occupied on the nights of 8th-9th April, Several horses died of exhaustion during the night and some had to be evacuated and destroyed during the morning. During the 3 days operation the regiment lost 23 horses (dead) owing to the weather and short forage.   (12,15)

    unit:3 Hussars (20,20)
    unit:Carabiniers (6 Dragoon Guards) (29,20)
    unit:Scots Greys (39,20)
    reference:Sercus, pas de calais, (?) 14th, 1917: The regiment addled up ready to move at 05:30. they moved off to  Y woods half a mile south of R of Sercus, where the brigade, less 3rd Hussars concentrated. The brigade marched to a position of readiness as ordered via Morbecque, Brigade H8, Le Grand Hazard. The  Carabiniers and oxford Hussars Papote. The brigade was directed to cover the left flank of the 1st Army in the event of a retirement. The enemy attacked three times during the day but were repulsed each time. One regiment - the Scots Greys - of 5th brigade - relieved the 3rd Hussars at 19:30 and the brigade withdrew into reserve at Sercus. Thirty nine remounts mounte by men of (the) dismounted party forward. Captain R. Kennefield R.A.M.C. left the regiment to proceed to England on termination of engagement. Captain R. Marshall R.A.M.C joined the regiment.  (11,21)

    reference:Papote, pas de calais, (?) 16th, 1917: The regiment had all saddles packed and stood to at 45 minutes notice from 07:30. The squadron leaders of 'A' and 'C' squadrons proceeded to Papote at 13:30 to take over positions of machines from 4th Hussars. The regiment paraded at 16:30 and proceeded to dispositions as follows: R headquarters and 'B' squadron - Papote. 'A' squadron - edge of wood 1 mile sout east of R headquarters. 'C' squadron - at edge of wood where canal at Nieppe enters Bois Clebert, close to Le Parc. 'a' squadron established liaison with second Australian brgiade. 'C' squadron with 95th and 13th brigades. Releif of 4th Hussars complete at 18:30. The horses remained saddled up during the night. (17,33)

    time:0500PM (22,33)
    activity:movement (80,35)
    activity:other (20,36)
    reference:Orders (61,36)
    reference:Bailleulval, pas de calais, france (Jun?)24th 1918: Got orders to move 03:25; to an area about Adinfer. The regiment to be backing regiment, having heard that the well at Coucelles had been poisoned with arsenic. The regiment moved off at 06:00 via Ransart - valley due south of Adinfer. We stayed here till 09:00, Lieutenant Hatton took over duties as Intelligence officer. The remainder of the brigade off-saddled but we remained saddled up. At 10:00 we received orders (to) continue to Ayette. Captain Kirby was sent to 3rd Cavalry brigade headquarters as Liaison officer. The regiment remained in the position with squadrons well-spaced out up north and south side of Ayette - Douchy-les-Ayette until we off saddled at 10:00. Saddled up at 12;00 and watered in douchy and remained saddled up. Ordered to return to Basseur at 18:00, arrived at 19:40.  (18,36)

Duties received at 15:30 to set off again to Contay as Corps Cavalry to 5th Corps, relieving the 8th Hussars. Moved off at 16:15 via Pommera-Grenas- Hurtebise Farm - Thiures-Marieux- Raincheval-toutencourt-Contay. Arrived in billets at 19:50 .  (11,67)

  9 Oct 1918 0
    unit:Guards Division (23,18)
    unit:Canadians (25,18)
    unit:24 Division (28,18)
    unit:Infantry (63,18)
    reference:Niergnes, nord, france, october 10th 1918: The regiment stood to at 06:00. Liaison patrols being sent to Guards division, on right; Canadians, on left; and 24th division , in front. At 06:30 information received from Liaison patrol with 24th division that enemy had withdrawn and infantry not in touch with him. Regiment moved off at 06:35 with one squadron advanced guard whose orders were to push on quickly and get in touch with enemy; to go north east via Awoignt, north of Carnieres towards Avesnes. Regiment made good progress. Advanced guard fired at from Avesnes but pushed on into village, capturing a few prisoners. Ridge north of Avesnes strongly held by enemy, so advanced squadron dismounted for action and held eastern outskirts of village at 09:30. Infantry came up and took over at 16:00. Enemy shelling had increased during the day and advanced squadron suffered some casualties, including one officer, Lieutenant Jones, and 4 men missing. This party had galloped after some Germans and had run into (a) machine gun nest. Regiment withdrew to Cagnoncle for the night.  (16,18)

    reference:Cagnoncles, nord, france, october 12th 1918: Regiment stood to off-saddled from 08:00. Usual liaison patrols went out at 09:00. Message by Divisional Relay from 24th division, said that enemy were withdrawing and infantry walking on. Regiment saddled up at once. 'C' squadron moved off at 09:25 to 09:00 touch with enemy, remainder of regiment followed shortly after and halted (at) 1000 yards west of Avesnes. Our Liaison patrol reported our infantry still only on edge of St. Aubert; so commanding officer went forward to 17th brigade headquarters and after consultation with Brigadiers and GSO1, 24th division, it was decided to have one squadron up and 9the) remainder to withdraw to Cagnoncles. 'C' squadron remained out, getting touch with enemy on high ground just west of Waussy and Montrecourt. The squadron withdrew to Carnoncles at 16:00 having handed over to infantry of 17th brigade. (14,59)
